TL;DR: 提出了HandelBot，一个结合仿真策略与快速自适应的双阶段方法，实现了高精度的双手机器人钢琴演奏。


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: 多指灵巧操作在机器人领域极具挑战，尤其是在高精度任务中，数据采集困难成为限制因素。现有的强化学习和仿真技术在毫米级任务上仍有较大性能差距，因此亟需新的方法提升机器人操作精度。

Method: 提出HandelBot框架，采用两步法：第一步通过结构化优化矫正仿真策略的空间对齐，具体是根据物理实验调整机器人手指关节；第二步利用残差强化学习自动学习细致的补偿动作。整个过程极大地降低了对真实世界训练数据的需求。

Result: 在五首常用钢琴曲的机器人硬件实验中，HandelBot实现了高精度的双手钢琴演奏。相较于直接使用仿真策略，演奏表现提升1.8倍，仅需30分钟真实交互数据。

Conclusion: HandelBot极大推动了机器人多指精密操作能力，表明结合仿真和快速自适应能够实现高效、高精度的机器人任务，尤其适用于复杂乐器演奏等高要求场景。

Abstract: Mastering dexterous manipulation with multi-fingered hands has been a grand challenge in robotics for decades. Despite its potential, the difficulty of collecting high-quality data remains a primary bottleneck for high-precision tasks. While reinforcement learning and simulation-to-real-world transfer offer a promising alternative, the transferred policies often fail for tasks demanding millimeter-scale precision, such as bimanual piano playing. In this work, we introduce HandelBot, a framework that combines a simulation policy and rapid adaptation through a two-stage pipeline. Starting from a simulation-trained policy, we first apply a structured refinement stage to correct spatial alignments by adjusting lateral finger joints based on physical rollouts. Next, we use residual reinforcement learning to autonomously learn fine-grained corrective actions. Through extensive hardware experiments across five recognized songs, we demonstrate that HandelBot can successfully perform precise bimanual piano playing. Our system outperforms direct simulation deployment by a factor of 1.8x and requires only 30 minutes of physical interaction data.

### [223] [HumDex:Humanoid Dexterous Manipulation Made Easy](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.12260)
*Liang Heng,Yihe Tang,Jiajun Xu,Henghui Bao,Di Huang,Yue Wang*

TL;DR: 本文提出了一种新型可移植的人形机器人全身灵巧操作远程控制系统HumDex，通过IMU运动追踪和平滑自然的手部重定向，实现高效、高精度的数据采集和泛化能力优良的模仿学习。


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: 当前人形机器人灵巧操作任务中，高质量演示数据采集效率低下是核心瓶颈。现有远程操控系统往往难以兼顾可移植性与精度，且容易受遮挡、精度不够等问题影响，阻碍其在复杂全身任务中的应用。

Method: 1）提出HumDex系统，结合IMU运动追踪，实现便携与精确的全身动作捕捉。2）针对手部控制，采用基于学习的手势重定向方法，无需手动参数调整即可生成流畅自然的手部动作。3）利用该系统高效采集人类动作数据，并提出两阶段模仿学习：先用多样人类数据预训练，获得一般化先验，然后用机器人数据微调，以缩小人机差异，实现精准操作。

Result: 实验表明，所提方案在新场景、新物体和新背景下，有更好的泛化能力，同时数据采集效率和成本也大幅降低。

Conclusion: HumDex系统为人形机器人全身灵巧操作提供了实用的数据采集与控制方案，通过两阶段模仿学习，有效提升了泛化能力和实际应用价值，全部代码和系统已开源，便于社区复现和推广。

Abstract: This paper investigates humanoid whole-body dexterous manipulation, where the efficient collection of high-quality demonstration data remains a central bottleneck.
  Existing teleoperation systems often suffer from limited portability, occlusion, or insufficient precision, which hinders their applicability to complex whole-body tasks. To address these challenges, we introduce HumDex, a portable teleoperation system designed for humanoid whole-body dexterous manipulation. Our system leverages IMU-based motion tracking to address the portability-precision trade-off, enabling accurate full-body tracking while remaining easy to deploy. For dexterous hand control, we further introduce a learning-based retargeting method that generates smooth and natural hand motions without manual parameter tuning. Beyond teleoperation, HumDex enables efficient collection of human motion data. Building on this capability, we propose a two-stage imitation learning framework that first pre-trains on diverse human motion data to learn generalizable priors, and then fine-tunes on robot data to bridge the embodiment gap for precise execution. We demonstrate that this approach significantly improves generalization to new configurations, objects, and backgrounds with minimal data acquisition costs. The entire system is fully reproducible and open-sourced at https://github.com/physical-superintelligence-lab/HumDex.

### [224] [$Ψ_0$: An Open Foundation Model Towards Universal Humanoid Loco-Manipulation](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.12263)
*Songlin Wei,Hongyi Jing,Boqian Li,Zhenyu Zhao,Jiageng Mao,Zhenhao Ni,Sicheng He,Jie Liu,Xiawei Liu,Kaidi Kang,Sheng Zang,Weiduo Yuan,Marco Pavone,Di Huang,Yue Wang*

Main category: cs.RO

TL;DR: 本文提出了Psi-Zero（Ψ_0）模型，通过分阶段训练方式，提升了类人机器人在复杂行走和操作任务中的能力，仅用较少数据就取得了显著性能超越。


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: 现有方法通过对人类与类人机器人混合数据的大规模联合训练，来提升类人机器人的操作能力，但由于人和机器人的运动学及动作特性差异显著，这类方法数据利用效率低、模型性能有限。针对这一不足，作者希望通过更高效的数据利用策略，显著提升模型表现。

Method: 本文提出分阶段训练范式：首先在大量高质量、自视角人类操作视频上自回归预训练VLM骨干网络，获得通用视觉-动作表示；随后在高质量真实类人机器人数据上用流式动作专家后训练，实现精确的机器人关节控制。同时强调与以前靠杂乱互联网视频或跨不同机器人主体混合数据的做法不同，仅用高质量人类视频和领域专用真实机器人数据就可大幅提升效果。

Result: 实验证明：只需约800小时人类视频和30小时机器人数据，Psi-Zero在多项任务中整体成功率超过基线方法40%以上，而这些基线方法依赖于超过10倍体量的数据。

Conclusion: 本文验证了高质量、分阶段训练的数据策略在类人机器人操作上的优越性，将开源数据处理与训练管线、基础模型和实时推理引擎，促进社区发展。

Abstract: We introduce $Ψ_0$ (Psi-Zero), an open foundation model to address challenging humanoid loco-manipulation tasks. While existing approaches often attempt to address this fundamental problem by co-training on large and diverse human and humanoid data, we argue that this strategy is suboptimal due to the fundamental kinematic and motion disparities between humans and humanoid robots. Therefore, data efficiency and model performance remain unsatisfactory despite the considerable data volume. To address this challenge, \ours\;decouples the learning process to maximize the utility of heterogeneous data sources. Specifically, we propose a staged training paradigm with different learning objectives: First, we autoregressively pre-train a VLM backbone on large-scale egocentric human videos to acquire generalizable visual-action representations. Then, we post-train a flow-based action expert on high-quality humanoid robot data to learn precise robot joint control. Our research further identifies a critical yet often overlooked data recipe: in contrast to approaches that scale with noisy Internet clips or heterogeneous cross-embodiment robot datasets, we demonstrate that pre-training on high-quality egocentric human manipulation data followed by post-training on domain-specific real-world humanoid trajectories yields superior performance. Extensive real-world experiments demonstrate that \ours\ achieves the best performance using only about 800 hours of human video data and 30 hours of real-world robot data, outperforming baselines pre-trained on more than 10$\times$ as much data by over 40\% in overall success rate across multiple tasks. We will open-source the entire ecosystem to the community, including a data processing and training pipeline, a humanoid foundation model, and a real-time action inference engine.

</details>
